## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the core problem of chemical reaction kinetics. The rate law typically depends on powers of concentration, and time-dependence may indicate external forcing or catalyst deactivation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law kinetics)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + A) (transition between reaction orders)
- Michaelis-Menten/saturation kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or surface-catalyzed reactions)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or activation over time)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Combined order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (competing first and second order pathways)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or fractal kinetics)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Square root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (dissociative adsorption-limited reactions)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer or half-integer power of concentration → classical reaction order reflecting molecularity of elementary steps
- Rational function of concentration (A/(1+A) forms) → surface-catalyzed or enzyme-mediated reaction with adsorption/binding equilibrium
- Negative sign of leading coefficient → consumption/decay of reactant species
- Product of concentration and (constant - concentration) → autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior in chemical systems
- Exponential dependence on time → time-varying external conditions such as temperature ramp or catalyst deactivation
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel reaction pathways with different orders
- Concentration in denominator squared → cooperative binding or substrate inhibition mechanisms
- Linear combination of A and A² without explicit time dependence → system governed purely by concentration-dependent rate law (autonomous ODE)
